## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics: nonlinear oscillations and dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration and the inputs are position x, velocity v, and time t, which matches second-order ODE models of oscillators written as x' = v, v' = dv_dt. Nonlinear harmonic oscillators typically express dv_dt as a restoring force in x plus damping in v and possibly external/parametric time-dependent forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear (Hookean) oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (small-amplitude conservative oscillations)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (damped harmonic oscillator)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (periodic external forcing)
- Driven with phase shift: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (general sinusoidal drive)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3) - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Duffing with forcing: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3) - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear resonance, bistability)
- Nonlinear damping (quadratic/cubic drag): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like drag); or dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (odd nonlinear damping)
- Pendulum-like restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (large-angle oscillations; sinusoidal restoring)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - x**2) * v - c2 * x (self-excited oscillations and limit cycles)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent self-excitation): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (negative linear damping stabilized by nonlinear damping)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness; parametric resonance)
- Conservative potential expansion: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) (generic polynomial approximation to -dU/dx near equilibrium)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd restoring-force symmetry: if the equilibrium is at x = 0 and the potential is symmetric, dv_dt often contains only odd powers of x (x, x**3, x**5) or sin(c*x), implying antisymmetry dv_dt(-x, -v) = -dv_dt(x, v).
- Energy-conserving vs dissipative structure: conservative models depend on x only (dv_dt = f(x)), while dissipation introduces terms proportional to v or odd functions of v (dv_dt includes -c*v, -c*v**3, -c*v*Abs(v)).
- Self-excitation/limit cycles: terms like (c0 - x**2)*v (Van der Pol) or v - v**3 (Rayleigh) indicate negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude, producing stable oscillations.
- Hardening/softening identification: adding +c*x**3 in the restoring force (i.e., dv_dt includes -c*x**3) changes frequency with amplitude; the sign of the cubic term distinguishes hardening vs softening behavior.
- Periodic forcing signature: additive sin/cos terms in dv_dt imply externally driven oscillations; responses show resonance when the forcing frequency matches the natural frequency.
- Parametric resonance signature: time-periodic multiplication of x (e.g., -(c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x) indicates stiffness modulation and can create instability tongues (Mathieu behavior).
- Non-smooth damping/friction: inclusion of Abs(v) or v*Abs(v) suggests Coulomb-like or quadratic drag effects, often leading to sharp changes near v = 0.
- Model-order consistency check: because x' = v, any explicit dependence dv_dt(x, v, t) should be interpretable as a force law; terms involving x*v can indicate state-dependent damping or gyroscopic-like coupling (in 1D typically nonlinear damping).

GT (fixed):  
\[
f(x,v)= -0.59954989233168\,v\;-\;2.79522534599104\,x\,e^{-|x|}
\]
Key structural facts:
- Depends on **v linearly** with a constant coefficient.
- The x-part is **non-polynomial** and **non-analytic at 0** because of \(|x|\): \(x e^{-|x|}\).
- No candidate includes `Abs(x)` or `exp(-Abs(x))` (or any equivalent piecewise construction), so the only way to match would be if candidates could *somehow* represent \(x e^{-|x|}\) exactly. Pure sums of monomials, logs, sin, exp(t), etc. cannot equal \(x e^{-|x|}\) for all real x.

GT: -c0*beta*v - omega0**c1*x*exp(-Abs(x))

I need to determine which candidates can exactly match the ground truth:

**GT: -0.59954989233168*v - 2.79522534599104*x*exp(-Abs(x))**

The key feature of the GT is the term `x*exp(-|x|)`. This is NOT a polynomial, NOT a power law, and NOT a simple trigonometric or logarithmic function. Let me analyze what `x*exp(-|x|)` looks like:

- For x > 0: `x*exp(-x)` â€” this is x times a decaying exponential
- For x < 0: `x*exp(x)` â€” this is x times a growing exponential (but x is negative)

This function cannot be represented as a finite sum of power-law terms `x^a`, polynomials, or standard elementary functions like `sin`, `cos`, `log` alone.

Now let me examine the candidates:

**All candidates (1-50)** are built from combinations of:
- Linear terms in x, v
- Power law terms: `x^c` (for various constants c)
- Polynomial terms: `x^3`, `x^5`
- Some have `log(...)`, `sin(...)`, `cos(t)`, `exp(c*t)`, `v^c`, `v*x^4`
- Some have `(c+x)^3`

**Critical analysis:** The function `x*exp(-|x|)` is an entire analytic function (on each half-line) that cannot be expressed as a **finite** sum of power-law terms `x^a`. A Taylor series would require infinitely many terms. Power-law terms `x^c` with non-integer c have branch-point singularities at x=0, while `x*exp(-|x|)` is smooth everywhere.

Let me check if any candidate has `exp(...)` of x:
- Candidate 45: has `exp(c5*t)` â€” exponential in t, not x
- No candidate has `exp(x)` or `exp(-x)` or `exp(-|x|)`

The candidates with `log` terms (18, 19, 44, 46, 48, 50) have `log(c*v+1)` or `log(c*x+1)`, which don't help create `exp(-|x|)`.

Candidate 9 has `sin(c3*x + c4)` â€” trigonometric, not exponential.

**None of the candidates contain `exp(-|x|)` or any mechanism to generate it.** Since `x*exp(-|x|)` is linearly independent from all finite combinations of power laws, polynomials, logarithms, and trigonometric functions, no candidate can match the GT.

Let me verify: Could a sum of power laws `x^a` approximate `x*exp(-|x|)` exactly? No â€” `x*exp(-|x|)` decays exponentially for large |x|, while any finite sum of power laws either grows or decays polynomially. They are fundamentally different function classes.
